Here are 10 facts you may or may not have known about Ankylosaurus." data-socialimage="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/2/h/-/-/ankylosaurusWC.JPG" data-socialtitle="How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?" data-url="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm" id="content">

           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              Ankylosaurus was the Cretaceous equivalent of a Sherman tank: low-slung, slow-moving, and covered with thick, nearly impenetrable armor. On the following slides, you'll discover 10 facts that you may or may not have known about this famous dinosaur.
             </p>

              <h2 class="heading ">
               Fact #1 - There Are Two Ways to Pronounce Ankylosaurus
              </h2>
             </div>
             <div class="pull-right">
              <div class="page-btns group small">
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link prev" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm">

                 </span>
                </a>

                 <span class="sprite arrow4-right">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>

            </div>
            <figure class="content-img">
             <div class="sbs-img-frame">
              <div class="sbs-prev-next-top">
               <div class="page-btns group small">
                <div class="col pull-left prev">
                 <a class="btn p-b-col ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step1">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-left">
                  </span>

                </div>
                <div class="col pull-right next">
                 <a class="ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step3">
                 </a>

                  <span class="sprite arrow5-right">

              <div class="sbs-img-wrapper expandable collapsed">
               <div class="content-img-wrapper no-caption">
                <div class="image-pinit-wrapper">
                 <img alt="ankylosaurus - Mariana Ruiz" class=" addPinit" data-description="How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?: Fact #1 - There Are Two Ways to Pronounce Ankylosaurus" itemprop="image" src="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/w/T/-/-/ankylosaurusMR.png"/>
                </div>

            <figcaption class="content-img-subtitle">
             <div class="content-img-caption">
              <span class="credit">
               Photo Credit: Mariana Ruiz
              </span>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </div>
           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              Technically, Ankylosaurus (Greek for "fused lizard" or "stiffened lizard") should be pronounced with the accent on the second syllable: ank-EYE-low-SORE-us. However, most people (including most paleontologists) find it easier on the palate to put the stress on the first syllable: ANK-ill-oh-SORE-us. Either way is fine--this dinosaur won't mind, as it has been extinct for 65 million years.
             </p>
            </div>

         <noscript class="sbs-3" data-hint="Fact #2 - The Skin of Ankylosaurus Was Covered with Osteoderms">
          <!-- &lt;![endif]-->
          <div class="sbs-active-container active-step-3">
           <div class="sbs-intro" id="contentIntro">
            <div class="row">
             <div class="col col-6">
              <span class="page-count">
               3
               <span class="page-count-divider">
                of
               </span>
               12
              </span>
              <h2 class="heading ">
               Fact #2 - The Skin of Ankylosaurus Was Covered with Osteoderms
              </h2>
             </div>
             <div class="pull-right">
              <div class="page-btns group small">
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link prev" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_2.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-left">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link next" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_4.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-right">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figure class="content-img">
             <div class="sbs-img-frame">
              <div class="sbs-prev-next-top">
               <div class="page-btns group small">
                <div class="col pull-left prev">
                 <a class="btn p-b-col ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step2">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-left">
                  </span>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="col pull-right next">
                 <a class="ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step4">
                 </a>
                 <span class="btn p-b-col">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-right">
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="sbs-img-wrapper expandable collapsed">
               <div class="content-img-wrapper ">
                <div class="image-pinit-wrapper">
                 <img alt="osteoderms - " class=" addPinit" data-description="How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?: Fact #2 - The Skin of Ankylosaurus Was Covered with Osteoderms" itemprop="image" src="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/6/v/-/-/ankylosaurusWC3.jpg"/>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </figure>
            <figcaption class="content-img-subtitle">
             <div class="content-img-caption">
              A pair of osteoderms (Wikimedia Commons).
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </div>
           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              The most notable feature of Ankylosaurus was the tough, knobby armor covering its head, neck, back and tail--pretty much everything except its soft underbelly. This armor was made up of densely packed osteoderms, or "scutes," deeply embedded plates of bone (which weren't directly connected to the rest of Ankylosaurus' skeleton) covered by a thick layer of keratin, the same protein as is contained in human hair and rhinoceros horns.
             </p>
            </div>
           </article>

          <div class="sbs-active-container active-step-4">
           <div class="sbs-intro" id="contentIntro">
            <div class="row">
             <div class="col col-6">
              <span class="page-count">
               4
               <span class="page-count-divider">
                of
               </span>
               12
              </span>
              <h2 class="heading ">
               Fact #3 - Ankylosaurus Kept Predators at Bay with its Clubbed Tail
              </h2>
             </div>
             <div class="pull-right">
              <div class="page-btns group small">
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link prev" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_3.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-left">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link next" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_5.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-right">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figure class="content-img">
             <div class="sbs-img-frame">
              <div class="sbs-prev-next-top">
               <div class="page-btns group small">
                <div class="col pull-left prev">
                 <a class="btn p-b-col ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step3">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-left">
                  </span>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="col pull-right next">
                 <a class="ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step5">
                 </a>
                 <span class="btn p-b-col">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-right">
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="sbs-img-wrapper expandable collapsed">
               <div class="content-img-wrapper no-caption">
                <div class="image-pinit-wrapper">
                 <img alt="ankylosaurus - Wikimedia Commons" class=" addPinit" data-description="How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?: Fact #3 - Ankylosaurus Kept Predators at Bay with its Clubbed Tail" itemprop="image" src="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/7/v/-/-/ankylosaurusWC4.JPG"/>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </figure>
            <figcaption class="content-img-subtitle">
             <div class="content-img-caption">
              <span class="credit">
               Photo Credit: Wikimedia Commons
              </span>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </div>
           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              The armor of Ankylosaurus wasn't strictly defensive in nature; this dinosaur also wielded a heavy, blunt, dangerous-looking club on the end of its stiff tail, which it could whip at reasonably high speeds. What's unclear is whether Ankylosaurus swung its tail to keep predators at bay (the most likely explanation), or if this was a
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="1" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/dailylifeofadinosaur/a/dinosexing.htm">
               sexually selected
              </a>
              characteristic--that is, males with bigger tail clubs had the opportunity to mate with more females.
             </p>
            </div>
           </article>

          <div class="sbs-active-container active-step-5">
           <div class="sbs-intro" id="contentIntro">
            <div class="row">
             <div class="col col-6">
              <span class="page-count">
               5
               <span class="page-count-divider">
                of
               </span>
               12
              </span>
              <h2 class="heading ">
               Fact #4 - The Brain of Ankylosaurus Was Unusually Small
              </h2>
             </div>
             <div class="pull-right">
              <div class="page-btns group small">
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link prev" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_4.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-left">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link next" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_6.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-right">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figure class="content-img">
             <div class="sbs-img-frame">
              <div class="sbs-prev-next-top">
               <div class="page-btns group small">
                <div class="col pull-left prev">
                 <a class="btn p-b-col ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step4">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-left">
                  </span>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="col pull-right next">
                 <a class="ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step6">
                 </a>
                 <span class="btn p-b-col">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-right">
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="sbs-img-wrapper expandable collapsed">
               <div class="content-img-wrapper ">
                <div class="image-pinit-wrapper">
                 <img alt="ankylosaurus - " class=" addPinit" data-description="How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?: Fact #4 - The Brain of Ankylosaurus Was Unusually Small" itemprop="image" src="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/8/v/-/-/ankylosaurusWC2.jpg"/>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </figure>
            <figcaption class="content-img-subtitle">
             <div class="content-img-caption">
              An Ankylosaurus skull (Wikimedia Commons).
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </div>
           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              As imposing as it was, Ankylosaurus was powered by an unusually
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="1" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/dinosaurbasics/a/dinosmarts.htm">
               small brain
              </a>
              --which was about the same size as that of its close cousin
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="2" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Stegosaurus.htm">
               Stegosaurus
              </a>
              , long considered to be the most dim-witted of all the dinosaurs. As a rule, slow, armored, plant-munching animals don't require much in the way of grey matter, especially when their main defensive strategy consists of flopping down on the ground and lying motionless!
             </p>
            </div>
           </article>

          <div class="sbs-active-container active-step-6">
           <div class="sbs-intro" id="contentIntro">
            <div class="row">
             <div class="col col-6">
              <span class="page-count">
               6
               <span class="page-count-divider">
                of
               </span>
               12
              </span>
              <h2 class="heading ">
               Fact #5 - A Full-Grown Ankylosaurus Was Immune from Predation
              </h2>
             </div>
             <div class="pull-right">
              <div class="page-btns group small">
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link prev" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_5.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-left">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link next" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_7.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-right">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figure class="content-img">
             <div class="sbs-img-frame">
              <div class="sbs-prev-next-top">
               <div class="page-btns group small">
                <div class="col pull-left prev">
                 <a class="btn p-b-col ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step5">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-left">
                  </span>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="col pull-right next">
                 <a class="ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step7">
                 </a>
                 <span class="btn p-b-col">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-right">
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="sbs-img-wrapper expandable collapsed">
               <div class="content-img-wrapper no-caption">
                <div class="image-pinit-wrapper">
                 <img alt=" - " class=" addPinit" data-description="How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?: Fact #5 - A Full-Grown Ankylosaurus Was Immune from Predation" itemprop="image" src="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/9/v/-/-/ankylosaurusRR.jpg"/>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </figure>
           </div>
           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              When fully grown, an Ankylosaurus adult weighed as much as three or four tons and was built close to the ground, with a low center of gravity. Even a hungry
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="1" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/carnivorousdinosaurs/p/tyrannosaurus.htm">
               Tyrannosaurus Rex
              </a>
              (which weighed more than twice as much) would have found it nearly impossible to tip over an adult Ankylosaurus and take a bite out of its soft belly--which is why late
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="2" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/dinosaurbasics/a/dinosaurages_4.htm">
               Cretaceous
              </a>
              theropods preferred to prey on Ankylosaurus hatchlings and juveniles.
             </p>
             <p class="cb-split">
             </p>
            </div>

           <div class="sbs-intro" id="contentIntro">
            <div class="row">
             <div class="col col-6">
              <span class="page-count">
               7
               <span class="page-count-divider">
                of
               </span>
               12
              </span>
              <h2 class="heading ">
               Fact #6 - Ankylosaurus Was a Close Relative of Euoplocephalus
              </h2>
             </div>
             <div class="pull-right">
              <div class="page-btns group small">
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link prev" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_6.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-left">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link next" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_8.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-right">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figure class="content-img">
             <div class="sbs-img-frame">
              <div class="sbs-prev-next-top">
               <div class="page-btns group small">
                <div class="col pull-left prev">
                 <a class="btn p-b-col ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step6">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-left">
                  </span>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="col pull-right next">
                 <a class="ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step8">
                 </a>
                 <span class="btn p-b-col">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-right">
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="sbs-img-wrapper expandable collapsed">
               <div class="content-img-wrapper ">
                <div class="image-pinit-wrapper">
                 <img alt="euoplocephalus - " class=" addPinit" data-description="How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?: Fact #6 - Ankylosaurus Was a Close Relative of Euoplocephalus" itemprop="image" src="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/i/o/-/-/euoplocephalus2WC.JPG"/>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </figure>
            <figcaption class="content-img-subtitle">
             <div class="content-img-caption">
              Euoplocephalus (Wikimedia Commons).
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </div>
           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              As armored dinosaurs go, Ankylosaurus is much less well-attested than
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="1" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/herbivorousdinosaurs/p/euoplocephalus.htm">
               Euoplocephalus
              </a>
              , a slightly smaller (but more heavily armored) North American ankylosaur that's represented by dozens of fossil remains, down to this dinosaur's scute-covered eyelids. But because Ankylosaurus was discovered first--and because Euoplocephalus is a mouthful to pronounce--guess which dinosaur is more familiar to the general public?
             </p>
            </div>
           </article>

          <div class="sbs-active-container active-step-8">
           <div class="sbs-intro" id="contentIntro">
            <div class="row">
             <div class="col col-6">
              <span class="page-count">
               8
               <span class="page-count-divider">
                of
               </span>
               12
              </span>
              <h2 class="heading ">
               Fact #7 - Ankylosaurus Lived in a Near-Tropical Climate
              </h2>
             </div>
             <div class="pull-right">
              <div class="page-btns group small">
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link prev" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_7.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-left">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link next" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_9.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-right">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figure class="content-img">
             <div class="sbs-img-frame">
              <div class="sbs-prev-next-top">
               <div class="page-btns group small">
                <div class="col pull-left prev">
                 <a class="btn p-b-col ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step7">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-left">
                  </span>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="col pull-right next">
                 <a class="ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step9">
                 </a>
                 <span class="btn p-b-col">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-right">
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="sbs-img-wrapper expandable collapsed">
               <div class="content-img-wrapper ">
                <div class="image-pinit-wrapper">
                 <img alt="jungle - " class=" addPinit" data-description="How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?: Fact #7 - Ankylosaurus Lived in a Near-Tropical Climate" itemprop="image" src="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/q/t/-/-/jungleWC.JPG"/>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </figure>
            <figcaption class="content-img-subtitle">
             <div class="content-img-caption">
              A jungle habitat (Wikimedia Commons).
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </div>
           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              During the late
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="1" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/dinosaurbasics/a/dinosaurages_4.htm">
               Cretaceous
              </a>
              period, 65 million years ago, the western United States enjoyed a warm, humid, near-tropical climate. Considering its size and the environment it lived in, it's extremely likely that Ankylosaurus possessed a
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="2" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/dinosaurcontroversies/i/warmblooded.htm">
               cold-blooded
              </a>
              (or at the very least homeothermic, i.e., self-regulating) metabolism, which would have allowed it soak up energy during the day and dissipate it slowly at night.
             </p>
            </div>
           </article>

         <noscript class="sbs-9" data-hint="Fact #8 - Ankylosaurus Was Once Known as " dynamosaurus="">

          <div class="sbs-active-container active-step-9">
           <div class="sbs-intro" id="contentIntro">
            <div class="row">
             <div class="col col-6">
              <span class="page-count">
               9
               <span class="page-count-divider">
                of
               </span>
               12
              </span>
              <h2 class="heading ">
               Fact #8 - Ankylosaurus Was Once Known as "Dynamosaurus"
              </h2>
             </div>
             <div class="pull-right">
              <div class="page-btns group small">
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link prev" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_8.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-left">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link next" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_10.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-right">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figure class="content-img">
             <div class="sbs-img-frame">
              <div class="sbs-prev-next-top">
               <div class="page-btns group small">
                <div class="col pull-left prev">
                 <a class="btn p-b-col ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step8">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-left">
                  </span>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="col pull-right next">
                 <a class="ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step10">
                 </a>
                 <span class="btn p-b-col">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-right">
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="sbs-img-wrapper expandable collapsed">
               <div class="content-img-wrapper no-caption">
                <div class="image-pinit-wrapper">
                 <img alt="ankylosaurus - Wikimedia Commons" class=" addPinit" data-description='How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?: Fact #8 - Ankylosaurus Was Once Known as "Dynamosaurus"' itemprop="image" src="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/A/v/-/-/ankylosaurusWC5.jpg"/>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </figure>
            <figcaption class="content-img-subtitle">
             <div class="content-img-caption">
              <span class="credit">
               Photo Credit: Wikimedia Commons
              </span>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </div>
           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              The "type fossil" of Ankylosaurus was discovered by the famous paleontologist (and P.T. Barnum namesake)
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="1" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/famouspaleontologists/p/barnumbrown.htm">
               Barnum Brown
              </a>
              in 1906, in Montana's Hell Creek formation.Brown went on to unearth numerous other Ankylosaurus remains, including scattered pieces of fossilized armor that he initially attributed to a dinosaur he dubbed "Dynamosaurus" (a name that has unfortunately vanished from the paleontological archives).
             </p>
            </div>
           </article>

              <span class="page-count">

              </span>
              <h2 class="heading ">
               Fact #9 - Dinosaurs Like Ankylosaurus Lived All Over the World
              </h2>
             </div>
             <div class="pull-right">
              <div class="page-btns group small">
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link prev" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_9.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-left">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link next" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_11.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-right">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figure class="content-img">
             <div class="sbs-img-frame">
              <div class="sbs-prev-next-top">
               <div class="page-btns group small">
                <div class="col pull-left prev">
                 <a class="btn p-b-col ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step9">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-left">
                  </span>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="col pull-right next">
                 <a class="ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step11">
                 </a>
                 <span class="btn p-b-col">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-right">
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="sbs-img-wrapper expandable collapsed">
               <div class="content-img-wrapper ">
                <div class="image-pinit-wrapper">
                 <img alt="saichania - " class=" addPinit" data-description="How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?: Fact #9 - Dinosaurs Like Ankylosaurus Lived All Over the World" itemprop="image" src="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/H/3/-/-/saichania.jpg"/>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </figure>
            <figcaption class="content-img-subtitle">
             <div class="content-img-caption">
              Saichania, an Asian ankylosaur (Wikimedia Commons).
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </div>
           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              Ankylosaurus has lent its name to a widespread family of plant-eating dinosaurs, the
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="1" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/typesofdinosaurs/a/ankylosaurs.htm">
               ankylosaurs
              </a>
              , which have been discovered on every continent except Africa. The evolutionary relationships of these armored dinosaurs is a matter of dispute, beyond the fact that ankylosaurs were closely related to
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="2" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/typesofdinosaurs/a/stegosaurs.htm">
               stegosaurs
              </a>
              ; it's possible that at least some of their surface similarities can be chalked up to
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="3" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="http://evolution.about.com/od/macroevolution/a/Convergent-Evolution.htm">
               convergent evolution
              </a>
              .
             </p>
             <p class="cb-split">
             </p>
            </div>
           </article>

              </h2>
             </div>
             <div class="pull-right">
              <div class="page-btns group small">
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link prev" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_10.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-left">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
               <div class="col">
                <a class="btn btn-circle ajax-link next" data-component="stepbystepArrows" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="StepContent_Pagination" data-type="pagination" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus_12.htm">
                 <span class="sprite arrow4-right">
                 </span>
                </a>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </div>
            <figure class="content-img">
             <div class="sbs-img-frame">
              <div class="sbs-prev-next-top">
               <div class="page-btns group small">
                <div class="col pull-left prev">
                 <a class="btn p-b-col ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Prev" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step10">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-left">
                  </span>
                 </a>
                </div>
                <div class="col pull-right next">
                 <a class="ajax-link-sbs" data-component="stepbystepImage" data-ordinal="Next" data-source="stepbystepImage" data-type="" href="http://dinosaurs.about.com/od/typesofdinosaurs/ss/10-Facts-About-Ankylosaurus.htm#step12">
                 </a>
                 <span class="btn p-b-col">
                  <span class="sprite arrow5-right">
                  </span>
                 </span>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="sbs-img-wrapper expandable collapsed">
               <div class="content-img-wrapper no-caption">
                <div class="image-pinit-wrapper">
                 <img alt="K/T meteor - NASA" class=" addPinit" data-description="How Much Do You Know About Ankylosaurus?: Fact #10 - Ankylosaurus Survived to the Cusp of the K/T Extinction" itemprop="image" src="http://f.tqn.com/y/dinosaurs/1/S/J/g/-/-/meteorWC.jpg"/>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
            </figure>
            <figcaption class="content-img-subtitle">
             <div class="content-img-caption">
              <span class="credit">
               Photo Credit: NASA
              </span>
             </div>
            </figcaption>
           </div>
           <article class="sbs content widget expert-content">
            <div class="expert-content-text">
             <p>
              The near-impenetrable armor of Ankylosaurus, combined with its presumed cold-blooded metabolism, enabled it to weather the
              <a data-component="link" data-ordinal="1" data-source="inlineLink" data-type="internalLink" href="/od/dinosaurextinction/a/meteorite.htm">
               K/T Extinction Event
              </a>
              better than most dinosaurs. Even still, Ankylosaurus populations slowly but surely died out 65 million years ago, doomed by the disappearance of the trees and ferns they were accustomed to munching on as vast clouds of dust circled the earth in the wake of the Yucatan meteor impact.
             </p>
             <p class="cb-split">
             </p>
            </div>
           </article>

function google_ad_request_done(google_ads) {
	var containerSelector = 'active-article',
		build = function(){
			debug.log('building the cpc links: afc/radlinks');
			Abt.AdCode.buildAdsenseAfc('&lt;a href="#" data-component="html" data-source="stepbystepPage" data-type="adsLabel" data-ordinal="1" onclick="javascript: var w=450, h=425, top=(screen.height / 2) - (h / 2), left=(screen.width / 2) - (w / 2); window.open(&#39;http://www.about.com/z/ad/wasl.htm&#39;, &#39;&#39;, &#39;width=&#39; + w + &#39;, height=&#39; + h + &#39;, top=&#39; + top + &#39;, left=&#39; + left + &#39;, toolbar=no, location=no, directories=no, status=no, menubar=no, scrollbars=yes, resizable=yes, copyhistory=no&#39;); return false;" class="muted"&gt;Ads&lt;/a&gt;', containerSelector);
			Abt.AdCode.buildRadlinks('dinosaurs', '&lt;a href="#" data-component="html" data-source="stepbystepPage" data-type="adsLabel" data-ordinal="2" onclick="javascript: var w=450, h=425, top=(screen.height / 2) - (h / 2), left=(screen.width / 2) - (w / 2); window.open(&#39;http://www.about.com/z/ad/wasl.htm&#39;, &#39;&#39;, &#39;width=&#39; + w + &#39;, height=&#39; + h + &#39;, top=&#39; + top + &#39;, left=&#39; + left + &#39;, toolbar=no, location=no, directories=no, status=no, menubar=no, scrollbars=yes, resizable=yes, copyhistory=no&#39;); return false;" class="muted"&gt;Ads&lt;/a&gt;', containerSelector);
		};

	if($('#stepbystepPage').length &gt; 0) {
		debug.log('SBS Page: wait until content has loaded');
		if($('#content').hasClass('loaded')) {
			debug.log('sbs page is loaded');

	} else {

	}
}
